Explorer Yang Jiake's Grand Tour 162

To Hunt for Rare Beasts in Kangzang

The Continental Daily News reports that Mr. Yang Jiake, an overseas Chinese from Honolulu, previously accompanied the son of the late American President Roosevelt on an expedition to hunt in India and Tibet. He has now been commissioned by the American Museum of Natural History in New York and funded by private scientists. He arrived in Shanghai again last week and will depart with three zoological explorers on the 15th of this month for Qinghai and Xikang. They plan to spend more than a year searching for snow leopards and rare mammals. It is said that snow leopards are native to the Tibetan Plateau and live in snow-covered areas rarely visited by humans, making them extremely difficult to hunt. Once captured, they will be displayed in the Roosevelt Memorial Hall of the Natural History Museum. In addition, they plan to go to the Jishi Mountains to hunt small mammals, from free-tailed rats to foxes, all of which are on the list. This area is the source of the Yellow River and has not yet been surveyed or explored by modern people. However, it is difficult to predict whether they will be able to penetrate this area and must depend on the local situation. If they can capture live animals, they will also be transported back for breeding. He now hopes to obtain the cooperation of the New York Municipal Museum and the Academia Sinica to enhance the expedition. Their route is planned to be by river steamer to Chongqing, then overland to Yazhou and Daqianlu, to retrieve equipment and supplies left over from last year's exploration of Xikang, before heading to Qinghai. If they can pass through the Jishi Mountains, they will take the Longhai Railway through Lanzhou and Tongguan back to Shanghai. Last year, when he accompanied four American youths on an expedition to Xikang, they climbed the 24,000-foot Daxue Mountain. After escorting them back to Shanghai, he returned to the Tibetan Plateau to collect golden monkeys, blue sheep, grizzly bears, leopard-like civets, and pandas. He even donated a giant panda to the North China Branch of the Royal Asiatic Society museum in Shanghai.

Rickshaw Boss Chen Dexing Assassinated 163

Six Robbers Arrive in the Dead of Night

Feud Made to Look Like Robbery

Chen Dexing, a native of Taizhou, 33 years old, lived at No. 5 Haiyuan Lane, at the end of Qingyun Road, Zhabei. He made a living by renting out rickshaws, so his income was not bad. In addition, Chen was diligent and frugal, so he had accumulated some wealth over the years. At around midnight the night before last, Chen Zhengfang was about to go to bed when he suddenly heard urgent knocking on the door outside. Chen thought it was a rickshaw puller returning from his shift, so he put on his clothes and got up to open the door. Unexpectedly, the visitors were not rickshaw pullers, but six bandits wearing short blue and black cloth shirts and pants, speaking with a Jiangbei accent. Before Chen could speak, one of the bandits in the middle pointed and said, "This is Boss Chen." Another bandit immediately took out a gun and fired two shots at Chen, one hitting his left leg and the other his lower abdomen. He immediately fell to the ground, blood gushing out like a spring, and died instantly. The murderers, seeing that their goal had been achieved, scattered and fled to the west. However, one bandit turned back before fleeing, barged into Chen's bedroom, threatened Chen's wife, Cai, not to make a sound, and stole a small leather suitcase before fleeing. Cai, seeing the bandits leaving, also chased after them, hoping to call for help. But she saw her husband lying on the ground and knew something was wrong. She quickly took a lamp to check and found that he had already died. She was greatly alarmed and rushed to the police station No. 46 of the 5th precinct on nearby Xibaoxing Road to report the crime. The sub-station was notified and dispatched a senior police officer to investigate the scene. It was learned that there was nothing in the stolen leather suitcase except for several account books. It was clearly a feud killing, disguised as a robbery afterward to cover it up. The station reported the case to the 5th District Headquarters and ordered the local bailiff to report to the court for an inquest yesterday morning. Meanwhile, detectives were dispatched to search for the murderers in all directions.

In addition to borrowing 1,000 yuan from her sister, Lu also pawned all her clothing and other items. Although she repeatedly negotiated, Lu enlisted friends Pan Mingzhi, Zhou Qifeng, and Zhu Houtian to negotiate with her, offering to return the diamond ring and repay 400 yuan, later increasing it to over 1,000 yuan. Because she had not seen Lu in person, she refused. She now requested the court to punish him according to the law and order him to return the cheated items and loans. When Lu Zhixin was questioned, he denied all of Yang Wenzhen's claims, saying that they had not had a relationship, had not lived together, and there had been no loans. Zheng Lupi, the second landlord of No. 44 Anle Lane, testified that she worked as an assistant at the Zhigong Law Firm and proved that Lu had come to rent the house on September 24 of last year, stating that the monthly rent was 60 yuan. Later, Lu and Yang Wenzhen moved in together. Judge Wu said that the case still needed to be investigated further and ordered a postponement until the 12th for further hearing. The defendant was ordered to provide a guarantor who could be summoned at any time, or be taken into custody if no guarantor was available.

The Genesis of the Shen Bao Reading Q&A Column 172

The Circulation Library attached to this newspaper is one of the ways our library serves the community. Its purpose is to supplement the inadequacies of news education and provide the general public with opportunities to gain knowledge. Since its establishment a year ago, according to recent statistics, an average of 600 readers borrow books every day, and the total number of registered readers is nearly 5,000. This shows that the establishment of the Circulation Library does indeed meet the urgent needs of the general public. However, according to another statistic, most of the library's readers are diligent and self-taught young people who, despite having access to books, still lack the guidance of teachers and friends and have no way to resolve their academic difficulties. Therefore, this library has specially created a [Reading Guidance] section to assist readers, and this newspaper has also specially added a [Reading Q&A] column to provide readers with a forum for questioning and solving doubts. This is an unprecedented initiative, and we sincerely hope that people from all walks of life will provide guidance and assistance to help us achieve our goal. The [Reading Q&A] regulations are attached below.

Reading Q&A Regulations 173

This column is based on the purpose of establishing [Reading Guidance] to allow readers to ask questions at any time. The scope of questions and answers is specifically defined as follows: 1. Questions about personal reading plans and reading methods; 2. Questions about each book, whether it is unclear words or phrases, or incomprehensible theories; 3. Research on the central idea of each book, or discussion of one's own critical opinions; 4. Collection of reference books. Within the above scope, this column will do its best to answer. If difficult questions are encountered, various specialized scholars will be specially invited to solve them. However, readers who submit letters to ask questions or still have doubts about the answers must strictly follow the following procedures: 1. All letters must indicate the number and name of the sender's library borrowing card and address. Readers from other cities can only write their name, gender, occupation, and education level; 2. For questions about the second item above, the letter must indicate the book, volume, page, author's name, and publishing bookstore; 3. The handwriting must be clear, preferably transcribed on manuscript paper printed by various bookstores. Do not write in pencil; 4. The wording of the questions should be concise, and the meaning of the discussion should also be concise, avoiding rambling and lengthiness; 5. If the answer in this column is still unclear or unsatisfactory, the second letter must first record the main points of the first answer and one's own questions and request guidance; 6. If the questions and answers cannot be clarified, readers can request a face-to-face meeting with [Reading Guidance] at the Shen Bao Circulation Library. If [Reading Guidance] deems it necessary, it can also send a letter to request a conversation; 7. All Shen Bao Reading Newspaper Offices are valid only if they have a [Reading Q&A] stamp, otherwise, no answers will be given; 8. Letters must be clearly marked with "Shen Bao Circulation Library [Reading Guidance] Receive" on the envelope and have sufficient postage stamps. If readers have any opinions on the above regulations, they can be modified at any time.

Letter Received 174

Dear Sir, After reading the report in your newspaper on the 1st of this month about Xie Fuzi and Fan Guozhen embezzling prisoners' rations and being sentenced to one year of imprisonment after the prosecutor's appeal, it is completely inconsistent with the original judgment. After investigation, the first instance of this case was declared not guilty, and the second instance also clarified that there was no embezzlement of prisoners' rations. The conviction was based on the point of using false information in official documents. A look at the judgment's main text shows that the part about the embezzlement of prisoners' rations was revoked. Xie Fuzi and Fan Guozhen jointly used false information in official documents and were each sentenced to 8

one year of imprisonment, and the rest of the appeal was dismissed. This can be clearly understood. As for the so-called use of false information in official documents, it refers to the fact that in the reported forms, the prisoners to be escorted on the next day were sometimes listed on the previous day. However, this was caused by a mistake in the registration by the female prison supervisors, and it has absolutely no impact on the actual payment and sales of prisoners' rations. Although supervisory officials at all levels are inevitably responsible for negligence, it does not constitute a criminal offense. In addition to applying for an appeal for relief in accordance with the law, we hereby send a special letter to your newspaper for correction in order to show the facts and protect our reputation. We are extremely grateful. Sincerely, Xie Fuzi and Fan Guozhen.

Education News

Special Feature

Report on the Ministry of Education Commissioner's Inspection of Education in Europe

Vocational Education Report 177

(II)

▲The Influence of Machine Industry: The development of machine industry means that a large number of workers are gathered in one place. The transmission of technology, if still in the form of apprenticeship, is difficult, and the products of the factory are timed. Teaching students must take a lot of time. To teach students, it takes a lot of time and losses will be significant if simultaneously held in the factory. Therefore, the training of students' technology must be separated from the factory, and there is a need to open classes and establish education. This is the beginning of organized vocational education, which is initiated by employers.

▲The Self-Consciousness of the Social Masses: Since the Industrial Revolution, the lives of workers in Europe have become more prosperous, and national education has gradually become popular. As a result, ordinary workers and low-level employees often feel that their own knowledge is insufficient as their knowledge increases day by day, and they need to improve their knowledge. In London, England, at the beginning of the 19th century, there were organizations such as Mechanics Institutes and Workingmens Colleges, all of which were automatically initiated by workers' groups. Later, there were workers' night schools and youth night schools. In the book "Industrial Education" by 8

Millis), there is the following paragraph about the development of 8

industrial education:

"At that time, there were two forces pushing forward. One was the workers' feelings about political and social instability, and the other was their desire to improve themselves and raise the status of their profession. Therefore, they were very concerned about the training of workers' skills and the training of young workers. They were especially eager for the scientific principles applied to their occupations. The vocational education movement was actually produced by these forces.] This is the original motivation for vocational education from the workers themselves.

▲The Competition in the World Economic Market: European countries, concerned about the benefits of vocational education, all believe that vocational education has a great relationship with the entire economic organization of the country. Because European countries, such as England, Germany, and Belgium, are all countries with excessive industrial production. The lifeblood of their domestic economy lies entirely in conquering the world market with their products. The key to whether they can sell their products to the world market lies entirely in the exquisiteness and applicability of their products, the reduction of costs, and the savings in transportation costs. All of these cannot be achieved without starting with good, complete, and organized vocational education. The Italian authorities said, ["The development of a country's industry requires several necessary conditions, such as raw materials, credit, merchant ships, the expansion of new markets, and indispensable skilled workers. If they are trained by schools using scientific and rational methods, the guarantee will be even more solid."] Millis also said, ["If a country's industry wants to occupy a position in the international market, it must rely on vocational education as a backing."] In 1883, England established the National Association For The*

Promotion of Technical Education). The main points of its declaration include the following (Note 2): (a) Any educational reforms that can enhance the skills of service personnel in the industrial sector should be encouraged. (b) The training of young people's hands and eyes should be stepped up. (c) The principles of science and arithmetic, which are the basis of national industry, should be made more popular.

["Industrial education is one of the essential elements of a country's economic lifeline. Our country (referring to Belgium) relies on the sale of industrial products to establish its status. If we do not strive to reduce the cost of our products, the danger is truly unimaginable. According to the teachings of experience, if we want to reduce costs, we must rely on excellent technology. If modern craftsmanship wants to win in the international arena, it must have technicians who have been trained in schools and are familiar with the latest methods to be driven by them to achieve results."] From this, it can be seen that European countries regard vocational education as the basis for their national life, and they all promote it without sparing any effort.

The current social and economic situation in our country, its exhaustion and poverty, has reached its extreme point. The reason for this can be summed up in one sentence, that is, the result of the dumping of industrial manufactured products from various countries. The annual leakage is huge, reaching tens of millions of dollars, which is the so-called economic aggression. The remedy is nothing more than two ways: 1. Resist foreign goods; 2. Establish manufacturing industries. The former is passive, unsustainable, and unnatural; the latter is a constructive national, positive, and hopeful path. Therefore, vocational education is an urgent task at present. However, the development of vocational education must have a suitable environment, just as fish must have water and plants must have rain and dew. Our primary, secondary, and higher education have not yet been put on the right track. It is difficult to demand perfection from vocational education alone. This is one reason. Vocational education is based on primary school education. When elementary education has not yet been completely organized, it is contrary to reason to seek satisfactory results from vocational education. This is the second reason. The authorities, although they know that vocational education is the only tool to resist economic aggression, whether they can appreciate its importance and implement it resolutely is the third reason. If the local government and the education authorities are slightly separated, the implementation will be weak and the results will be limited. This is the fourth reason. With these four reasons, it is difficult to develop vocational education in our country as much as possible in a short period of time. Other matters, such as the method of promotion and the raising of funds, are secondary matters. The following briefly lists the scope of vocational education and its relationship with social economy and local needs in order to clarify the general meaning of vocational education. The current situation of vocational education in various European countries will be described in detail in the next chapter.

I. The Scope of Vocational Education 178

Vocational education is closely related to adult continuing education and specialized education, and it is often difficult to distinguish them. Among the schools in our country that are close to vocational nature, in addition to the three types of commerce, agriculture, and engineering, there are also schools of telecommunications, medicine, pharmacy, merchant shipping, and fine arts. Foreign schools that use the name "vocational" are also numerous and difficult to name. Therefore, the scope of vocational education is particularly difficult to determine. Roughly speaking, there are the following categories:

(1) Agricultural schools, such as agriculture, forestry, animal husbandry, fruits and vegetables, sericulture, brewing, horticulture, and rural economics;

(2) Commercial schools, in addition to general commercial courses, there are also vocational courses for service in embassies and consulates abroad;

(3) Engineering schools, such as mechanical, electrical, architectural, textile, mining, and chemical engineering;

(4) Trade Schools

Catering, sewing, hat making, home economics, hairdressing, cooking, interior decoration, ceramic embroidery, machine installation, ironwork, locksmithing, woodworking, jewelry making, goldsmithing, engraving, printing, shoemaking, watchmaking, machine tool manufacturing, etc.

(5) Maritime schools, such as driving and engines;

Commercial schools and engineering schools are also collectively referred to as Trade Schools, and SchoolsofArtsondCrafts is sometimes used to include a part of engineering schools and trade schools. Therefore, in terms of names, it is not easy to analyze the categories of vocational schools and not confuse them. The above five categories are only general.

II. Vocational Education and Social Economy and People's Lives 179

The report of the League of Nations Education Inspection Team contributed a lot to the reform of education in our country. The two points that it repeatedly and earnestly said are: (1) The curriculum of our schools is too far from the actual lives of the people; (2) The secondary school curriculum should not be exclusively for students preparing to enter universities. In the section on vocational education, it also said,

["Chinese education should be more practical, and should especially focus on vocational education and specialized education. This report has been repeatedly voiced before and after."]

Politicians in various European countries have high vision and foresight, knowing that the enrichment of national economic strength is not only about the people having enough food and clothing, but also about expanding the world market to sell their surplus production. The wider the market, the more sales, the more the people will gain, and the more powerful the financial resources will be. Their success is all based on vocational education. In our country, if we can also plan to expand the world market and absorb foreign resources to adjust the domestic financial difficulties, it is certainly urgent. However, except for raw materials, it is by no means possible within a few decades for our country, which lags behind in machine manufacturing industry, to compete with various countries with manufactured products. According to the current situation in our country, the first step in vocational education, in addition to the necessary machine industry, should be to maintain our country's inherent handicrafts. The poverty of the country is often proportional to the number of idlers and unemployed in the country. The more idlers increase and the fewer producers decrease, the more parasites there will be, and the national strength will inevitably be exhausted. This is an inevitable principle. Giant cities and large ports in the country are dens of bandits and thieves, and beggars gather. They neither produce nor cause trouble. The loss to the country is difficult to calculate. In rural villages and small towns, due to the collapse of the rural economy, the old handicrafts are declining day by day, and the number of unemployed is increasing day by day. This is the greatest hidden danger of the country. If this is not cured for a long time, the national economic bankruptcy can be seen immediately. The current urgent need, in addition to maintaining public order with political power on the one hand, so that the people can live and work in peace, is to use educational methods to increase production and improve technology, so that rural undertakings can gradually recover and handicrafts will not be completely eliminated. Social economy and people's lives are closely related to vocational education. The Belgians have a saying, ["The British are rich in automatic spirit, and the French are rich in aesthetic ideas, but in the end, they are not as good as the Germans' good technical education and the power of great people. Therefore, Germany has today's superior economic position in the world."] In the fierce whirlpool of modern economic warfare and economic aggression, if our country does not work hard on industrial and vocational education in order to gain a foothold, all new and old production undertakings in the country will be squeezed and ravaged day by day, and it will be seen that they will decline and perish. The danger is unimaginable.

III. Vocational Education Must Meet the Needs of the Locality 180

There are currently no fewer than 300 national, provincial, and private vocational schools in our country. According to the types, there are industry, agriculture, commerce, medicine, music, fine arts, law and politics, fisheries, salt affairs, customs, postal affairs, telecommunications, merchant shipping, and police affairs. However, schools for customs, salt affairs, postal affairs, telecommunications, and police affairs are not only abnormally specialized in nature, but also have a very weak relationship with direct production. Therefore, vocational schools that have a direct relationship with the national economy should be schools of industry, agriculture, and commerce. Professor Svadkovsky of Soviet Russia told us in his book [Soviet Education] that 80% of the schools in the Soviet Union are engineering vocational schools, and 95% of the students in the country are in engineering vocational schools. According to French statistics, 80% of the people in the country serve in the agricultural, commercial, and industrial sectors. Therefore, it can be imagined that the most urgent need for vocational schools is agricultural, industrial, and commercial courses. The situation in other countries in the world is similar. When vocational schools for agriculture, commerce, and industry in our country are established, the automatic power of the provinces and local governments is greater. Therefore, the location of the schools can be distributed in the provinces, but the environment of the schools in the provinces is very different from the local industry and commerce and the supply of raw materials, but the departments established by the schools are all roughly the same, and the location of agricultural schools is not the center of rural undertakings. Therefore, most of the students are not 8

children of farmers, and after graduation, they do not serve in rural areas or engage in farming and animal husbandry. Therefore, the original reason is that agricultural schools lose their purpose of establishment and lose their effectiveness. They neither contribute to the agricultural undertakings on the technical front nor introduce talents. It seems equal to a fictitious establishment. Engineering schools and craft schools mostly favor new European and American crafts, and there are few who promote our country's old crafts. That is, they focus more on machine industry and ignore handicrafts. For example, mechanical engineering, electrical engineering, and civil engineering are established by almost all schools, and there are several schools that also establish applied chemical engineering courses. In our country, where the basic chemical industry has no foundation, it is appropriate that the employment and service problems of students after graduation are always the most difficult problems for schools. On the contrary, the businesses that are needed for people's daily life or the inherent special industries in various provinces and regions, such as furniture and utensils manufacturing, brick and tile lime manufacturing, bamboo and rattan ware industry, hardware tool industry, as well as the porcelain industry, pottery industry, lacquerware industry, leather industry, embroidery industry, ivory carving industry, etc., all have a foundation and a great social demand, but they lack specialized schools to provide research and no specialized courses to train technical talents. Therefore, the arts of various industries are sealed in the old steps and there is no progress at all. Moreover, there is a trend of decline. The University of Copenhagen in Denmark, which specializes in the porcelain engineering department due to the Royal Porcelain Factory, is ashamed. In summary, the existing vocational schools in our country, with a few exceptions, have one or more of the following shortcomings: 1. The departments established do not meet the needs of the special circumstances of the locality; 2. The location of the establishment is not entirely suitable; 3. The equipment is not complete; 4. The teaching materials are not practical; 5. The old handicrafts in our country are ignored. Or it is said that the old-fashioned crafts in our country have always been taught by masters and apprentices, and there is no need to set up schools to teach them. This is not entirely true. The old-fashioned crafts in our country often regress and make little progress because they stick to the old ways. In various European countries, all craft disciplines are based on art, so the style, color matching, etc. of the finished products all have artistic ideas and are suitable for the psychology of ordinary people, so sales are smooth and the business is growing. This is one of the most important points in craft technology. A French vocational educator said,

["Craftsmanship should meet the needs of the times and the economy and cultivate its talents. Therefore, it is flexible and requires students to pay attention to the economic conditions of all parties in the sales of products, so it is also progressive."] The [European Craft Schools] published by the British Ministry of Education also stated that ["Craft schools must pay attention to the changes and needs of the industrial sector." ] The biggest reason why vocational education in our country has not been able to show excellent results in the past is that it has not paid attention to the changing circumstances and needs of the industrial sector and the economic conditions of all parties. In other words, it is not suitable for local needs. Therefore, the employment of graduates is often a big problem, or they are idle and useless, or they change to other industries. The credibility and status of vocational schools in society are greatly damaged. Therefore, it is the first essential that vocational schools must meet the needs of the locality. (Note 1) The vocational schools run by the Shanghai Chinese Vocational Education Society and the provincial vocational schools in various provinces also have achievements, but the number is small. (Note 2) See the book "TradeSchoolsontheContinnet" published by the British Ministry of Education.

International Convention on the Circulation of Educational Films: Our Country Does Not Sign 184

According to the report of Minister Hu Shize of Switzerland, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stated that our country has few exported films, so if we sign the International Convention on the Circulation of Educational Films, we will only have obligations and no rights. (Many films from various countries are transported to China. If we do not sign, we will collect taxes as usual. After we sign, films from other countries will be tax-free, but our country has no films to export to exempt our taxes) and other information, consulted the Ministry of Education to reply to whether our country should sign. After the Fire at Peiping Normal University, Li Zheng Telegraphs the Ministry of Education to Request Punishment 185

▲Compensation Considered for Losses of Affected Students

(Special dispatch from Peiping) Following the fire in the Third Study Room of the College of Science at Normal University, Principal Li Zheng telegraphed the Ministry of Education to request punishment. Today (the 4th), the university posted a notice instructing affected students to list their lost items and submit them to the Dormitory Affairs Office for verification. Simultaneously, the affected students also held a meeting to discuss solutions. Principal Li Zheng scheduled a university affairs meeting at 3:00 PM on the 5th at the Office of the College of Liberal Arts. Dean of the College of Liberal Arts, Li Jinxi; Dean of the College of Science, Liu Tuo; Dean of the College of Education, Li Jianxun; Principal Li Zheng; and Secretary Yi Jia, among others, attended to discuss solutions to the fire's aftermath, including compensation for student losses and future fire prevention plans. It is said that these matters will be discussed together. It was discovered that the fire at the College of Science of Normal University occurred at 1:00 PM on the 2nd. At 1:20 PM, Principal Li Zheng, Secretary Yi Jia, and Wang Ruchuan heard the news and rushed to investigate. At the time, the fire was raging. Because the fire scene was very close to the library, Li and others, on one hand, assisted in extinguishing the fire and, on the other hand, protected the library and the various laboratories of the College of Science. With the assistance of the fire brigade, a major disaster was averted. Twenty-four rooms of the Third Study Room and three grey sheds of the Physics Laboratory were burned. These buildings were insured with the British Taikoo Fire & Marine Insurance Company in Tianjin for a total of 4,000 yuan, with 3,000 yuan for the Third Study Room and 1,000 yuan for the Physics Laboratory. It is estimated that the value of books, notes, and laboratory equipment inside the study room is around 50,000 yuan.

Today's Xilian Football Game: Youyou vs. French Business Association 196

2:30 PM at the Baseball Field

▲Draw for the Quarterfinals of the International Cup Has Been Made

▲China vs. Jewish, England vs. Soviet Union

Today, Xilian's Youyou team will play against the French Business Association in a Group A match at the China Baseball Field. Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Radio Psychometry Device 206

— Ming Xiang

Recently, British scientist Major Philip created a very interesting radio instrument called the Radio Psychometry Device. This is the first application of radio to psychology, and its reputation has spread to various countries. I will describe it to enlighten readers.

This device is extremely sensitive. Anyone who approaches it will cause an effect. The effect is even more pronounced when a hand approaches a pre-set copper plate. Previous explanations for this phenomenon attributed it to the human body's capacitance, which alters the inter-electrode capacitance between the grid and filament in the vacuum tube, thus changing the output plate current. However, Major Philip refutes this explanation, stating that recent radio scientists have used sophisticated instruments to prove that an electric field exists around the human body. He suggests that many phenomena in radio communication, previously attributed to human body capacitance, may actually be due to the effects of this electric field.

We all know that the human body's resistance changes with a person's actions and emotions. Precise instruments can record this change when a person experiences a sudden shock. Therefore, the so-called capacitance effect may be another phenomenon altogether, which seems reasonable.

The diagram shows the circuit of this device as tested by American radio scientists. It closely resembles a typical audio frequency amplification circuit, using a screen grid tube as the input tube, fed through a high-impedance primary audio frequency transformer to a triode output tube. The input tube's grid circuit is open, with only a copper plate connected to the grid. When a hand is placed near this plate, the output tube's plate current changes. The ammeter indicating this plate current can be a sensitive milliampere meter connected in parallel with the output transformer's primary winding. To ensure clear recordings, it is best to connect a 4.5V C battery and a 0.5 Meg variable resistor across the ammeter to block the original plate current from passing through the meter. Further adjust the variable resistor to set the original plate current reading to zero when the device is in use. The potentiometer R is used to adjust the stability and sensitivity of the measuring device.

When using this device, an additional device must be added to ensure that the distance between each test subject's hand and the copper plate is exactly the same, so the results obtained can be accurate. The results of the experiment have not yet been published, but it is believed that because different people can measure different results, based on these different results, humans can be divided into several categories according to their nervous temperament or mental activity. This issue is now open to the public, and experiments are welcome, and the conclusion of the experiment is even more anticipated.

Direct-Reading Vacuum Tube Voltmeter 207

— Li Yuanqing

Ordinary AC voltmeters can only be used to measure AC voltages with extremely low frequencies. If you use it to measure audio frequency or radio frequency voltages, it will not be applicable.

There is a type called a thermoammeter, which is constructed using the principle of thermal expansion and contraction. When current passes through a conductor, it heats up, and the conductor expands when heated, which can push the pointer of the ammeter. This kind of ammeter is very accurate in measuring currents of any frequency. However, in electricity, heat is proportional to the square of the current (L²R). If the current is too small, it cannot push the pointer, so this kind of meter is ineffective in measuring voltage.

Since the invention of the triode vacuum tube, people have used it to make high-frequency voltmeters. This kind of meter consumes very little external power when used, so the obtained value is exceptionally accurate.

Looking at Figure 1A, you can see the relationship between the triode vacuum tube's grid voltage and plate current. When the grid voltage is negative five volts, the plate current is reduced to zero. At this time, if the grid is connected to an external positive voltage, the plate current will increase. If it is connected to a negative voltage, the plate current will remain at zero. Observe the diagrams abcd··· and ABCD etc. to understand clearly. If the high-frequency voltage is connected to the plate, the obtained plate current will be shaped like 1, 2, etc. This kind of unidirectional current will of course cause the milliampere meter in the plate circuit to move. (See Figure 1B)

Figure 1A

Figure 1B is the wiring diagram of the vacuum tube voltmeter. When the external high-frequency voltage is connected to points XX, the ammeter connected in series in the plate circuit will have a reading. The magnitude of the plate current can be used to infer the magnitude of the external voltage.

Although the above-mentioned vacuum tube voltmeter is extremely simple in construction, various AC voltages of known values must be measured in turn beforehand, and then a curve diagram of the external voltage and plate current must be drawn before the value can be calculated according to the diagram. In addition, the values of C voltage and B voltage must be absolutely the same, otherwise the obtained record will not be accurate.

In order to avoid the above-mentioned difficulties, there is another type called a Slideback Vacuum Tube Voltmeter. The C voltage can be adjusted arbitrarily. As a result, the value of the external voltage can be directly calculated in the grid voltmeter V.

In Figure 2B, R1 is a potentiometer of considerable value. Before use, adjust R1 to make the plate current value zero. (At this time, the value of the grid C voltage is assumed to be E1.) When the external AC voltage E is connected at XX, the plate current will inevitably increase (such as the state in Figure 1A 1, 2, etc.). Then adjust R1 to reduce the plate current value to zero again. At this time, the C voltage must be greater than E1. (Such as Figure 2A E2). According to the AC voltage formula, the increased value (E2-E1) multiplied by 1.414 is equal to the effective value of the external AC voltage.

For example, the initial C voltage E1 is ten volts. After the external high-frequency voltage E is connected, the C voltage E2 increases to twenty volts. According to the above formula, we get:

External high-frequency voltage E = (20 - 10) X 1.414 = 14.14 volts (effective value)

The Key to Private Radio - Ultra-Short Waves 208

— Cai Guanghua

Today in the twentieth century, whether in war or in peacetime, the transmission of private messages is entirely in the hands of amateur experimenters of ultra-short waves. We know that the distinction of wavelengths is relative, not absolute. Wavelengths below ten meters are so-called ultra-short waves. From ten meters to two hundred meters is a wavelength range used by both police and amateurs. Next is the broadcasting range, and then all the way up to twenty thousand meters are long waves.

After short waves are transmitted, they refract on the surface of the sky and the earth. This refraction altitude is roughly one mile. However, the properties of ultra-short waves are different. After they are transmitted, they do not refract back. Where exactly they go is still an elusive thing. To transmit ultra-short waves, the transmitting and receiving machines must be on the same horizontal line (speaking of private communications).

[Beamcasting] is a specialized term used in ultra-short waves. The method is to transmit speech or music from a weak and invisible beam of light. Dr. D. I. E. Mouromtseff of Westinghouse Radio Company in the United States recently built one, using a wavelength of 109 meters, and performed a demonstration experiment. During beamcasting, he concentrated the .09-meter ultra-short wave on a parabolic mirror, and then concentrated the light from the mirror itself into a long and narrow shape (mostly parallel, and not diffuse). At the same time, inside the ultra-short wave radio receiver, there is also a parabolic mirror that concentrates the light on an antenna less than two inches long. Because the path the light travels is a straight line, this kind of transmission is on the same plane. However, if this equipment is set up higher above the ground, the range can be increased somewhat, which is certain. Therefore, high-rise buildings and the tops of towers and mountain tops are the best locations for beamcasting. Dr. Meng's machine performed well when tested at around one mile. He guessed that reception should also be possible at twenty miles. He said that if the army set up such a device, it would be much more private for transmitting messages. He hopes that the range can be increased further in the near future, so that the time for practical use will not be far off.

Portable Power Supply 209

— BF

The power supply described here is manufactured based on the principle of a vibrator transformer. (Please refer to the article "How to Use Transformers for DC Power" in Issue 42 of this publication.)

It can convert low-voltage DC power into high-voltage DC power for plate high-voltage current. This device is simple in construction and can also be connected to AC power lines.

This device connects a common small power transformer, rectifier, and filter in the usual way. Add a six-volt storage battery and a Ford spark coil (Zurich spark coil) connected in series with the storage battery to an unused five-volt coil on the power transformer. The wiring is shown in the attached diagram.

The two sides of the center tap of the power transformer each have three hundred volts. The power supply shown in the diagram can be used directly to supply a small power transmitter. If you want to use it for a radio, you must add a filter choke and an eight-microfarad fixed capacitor: and place the spark coil in the device in a grounded metal box. If this device is used where there is AC power, simply connect the primary of the power transformer to the power line.

The current required for the cathode of the vacuum tube in the machine can also be obtained from this power supply. It is simpler to use a current-type or energy-saving vacuum tube to supply the cathode current with a storage battery or dry battery.

Properties of Ultra-Short Waves 210

— VT

The wavelengths of ordinary radio stations are mostly from two hundred meters to six hundred meters. Those longer than this are long waves. Those shorter than this are short waves. After many years of research, it is known that short wavelengths are best suited for long-distance communication. In particular, around 20 meters is suitable for daytime, and around 40 meters is suitable for nighttime. This is due to reflection by the ionosphere. Ten meters or even one meter or less are specifically called ultra-short waves. Their properties are still under research and experimentation. Marconi, who came to China at the end of last year, is working even harder on research. He has done various experiments in the field and already knows that the reflection and refraction of these ultra-short waves are more significant than those of short waves. Therefore, it is often possible to use parabolic reflectors to focus them into a beam and transmit them in a single direction.

The properties of radio waves with a wavelength of less than one meter are almost identical to those of light rays. Therefore, they are also called optical radio waves. We know that the installation of a searchlight is to use a parabolic mirror installed behind the light emitter. The light rays emitted by the light emitter are reflected by the parabolic mirror and then proceed in a single direction. The light power is not lost and can directly illuminate the distance. Similarly, ultra-short waves can also use metal to create parabolic reflecting antennas or reflectors to focus the radio waves into a beam and transmit them in a single direction. At this time, the radio waves are not scattered like ordinary radio waves. Although the power is small, it can directly reach the distance. If a reflector is also used at the receiving end to focus the incoming parallel radio waves on the focal point, the transmitted information can be recovered. This is the point that Marconi is constantly researching.

Several years ago, a light telephone experiment was conducted between the English Channel and the French Channel. It is said to be very effective. This kind of light ray is called MicroRay and is also a type of extremely short radio wave. The antenna used in the experiment was less than one inch long, and the power used was as small as that used in an ordinary flashlight. It is already possible to communicate between two places separated by unobstructed objects. However, how to make these radio waves penetrate obstacles such as hills and buildings, etc., still needs to be researched.

In recent years, research on ultra-short waves has made great progress, and Marconi is a well-known researcher of ultra-short waves. Previous issues of this publication have already introduced this in domestic and foreign news, which you can refer to. If ultra-short waves can be practically used in local communications, it can save electricity and limit the distribution of information (because it is in a single direction). The radio world will usher in a revolution again.

It is not difficult to send and receive ultra-short waves of five meters to seven meters, but the distance is not far. The method will be introduced later. Now, taking advantage of the arrival of inventor Marconi in China, I will briefly describe the so-called name, properties, and reflective antenna principles of ultra-short waves to see the latest research in the radio world. It is hoped that domestic radio comrades can also rise up and catch up.

Sensitive Crystal Radio 211

— Ye Decan

This circuit diagram is from an American daily mechanical magazine. As a result of the experiment, the sound volume is very loud, and the selectivity is particularly sensitive. It may be more excellent than the excellent crystal radio introduced by Mr. Chun Tong in the 39th issue of this publication. And it is very convenient to manufacture. If a beginner can make one according to this, then all the components except the ore (except for the regenerative radio) can be used when you want to convert it into a one-tube radio.

The parts used are also very simple. The coil L is wound with No. 26 enameled wire on a plastic tube with a diameter of one and a half inches (so as to increase its radio receiving ability when retrofitting a one-tube radio) or a paper tube with 94 turns. L1L2 is wound with No. 32 enameled wire on the same plastic tube, and its diameter is one and a quarter inches. L1 is 107 turns, L2 is 17 turns: the two coils are a quarter inch apart. C can use .0005Mfd, C1 is .00035Mfd, and C2 uses .002Mfd.

Shen Bao Radio Weekly Department

Common Knowledge

(21) Vacuum Tube Radio (1) 213

— Huang Jiancun

(1) Classification of Vacuum Tube Radios: There are many types of vacuum tube radios. Looking at those sold on the market, there are so-called [several-tube radios] [certain type], etc. Counting them, there are no less than dozens of types. But if they are classified according to the different power supplies, they are nothing more than [DC radio] and [AC radio]. The so-called [DC type] is the one that uses dry batteries or storage batteries for its power supply, while the [AC type] uses AC power from electric lights as its power supply. When broadcast radio was in its infancy, all vacuum tube radios were DC type. Later, due to the feeling of various inconveniences of the DC type, such as the trouble of charging the A battery and the excessive consumption of the B battery, they worked hard to study and finally invented the AC radio. Once the AC type came out, the previous DC type was almost eliminated. In urban areas, the DC type is limited to portable or special mobile use (such as radios in trains and cars).

There are various distinctions between the two major categories of DC and AC radios. The simplest is due to the classification of the number of vacuum tubes, such as calling three-tube radios, five-tube radios, etc., and so on. Although this classification method is extremely simple, there are various methods in the same three-tube radio, and there are also differences in advantages, disadvantages, and functions, so the classification method based on the number of tubes is quite important. If you want to most appropriately indicate the type of vacuum tube radio, you must note the number of vacuum tubes on the one hand, and also note the certain method at the same time.

One thing to note in the classification by the number of vacuum tubes is that on the same machine, the AC radio requires one more tube than the DC radio, that is, the rectifier vacuum tube, which converts the AC power on the power line into DC power.

Page 16

Free Talk

Influence 214

— Yu Yangling

Artzybasheff said in a letter to a friend:

[People here often think that Nietzsche has had a great influence on me. This surprised me, the simplest reason being that I have never read Nietzsche. I do not sympathize with this prominent thinker, partly in his thoughts and partly in the flamboyant appearance of his works. I stopped reading his book as soon as I started.]

According to some literary critics, Gorky's novels about vagrant life seem to have been influenced by Nietzsche's doctrine. But according to Gorky himself, what influenced him more than the several books about Nietzsche's doctrine he read later was a conversation with a policeman named Nikiforych. At that time, Russian police were the most universally hated and despised, but in this Nikiforych's conversation, there were quite a few points that coincided with the German philosopher's views.

A writer who rejected Nietzsche, and a policeman who may not know Nietzsche's surname, both had Nietzsche's influence seen in their works and conversations, which seems incomprehensible. But the solution is not difficult, just look at the other commonalities of these people.

Gorky is an out-and-out Vadabond, needless to say how a police officer in the Tsarist era was a product of life, which is not difficult to imagine. Artzybasheff, on the other hand, had inherited tuberculosis from his mother since childhood and was poor, [living in a dirty attic without sufficient food.] As for Nietzsche, he had enlisted in the army, and he had also wandered around with a weak body. Like Gorky's university, his [cultural museum] was the whole of Europe.

Consciousness is ultimately a product of existence. How you live determines how you think and what theories you hold. If you have the same life, you will produce the same thoughts. From this point of view, it is natural that some of the thoughts of Gorky, Artzybasheff, Nikiforych, etc. can coincide with Nietzsche.

Ancient books are difficult to read, and philosophy books are even more difficult to read; Nietzsche's philosophy books are particularly difficult to read. If someone wants to understand Nietzsche and goes to read [Thus Spoke Zarathustra] and other books, it is really a difficult and stupid thing. Gorky said that few of the ideas he saw in books were not what he had already heard in real life. But the knowledge in books is ultimately empty talk on paper, far less than the things observed and experienced in real life. Rich in true and active qualities.

How to Study [Art History]? 215

— Tang Jun

Generally, people who read Western art history either find it [bland and uninteresting] or feel like they are [walking through mud]! Apart from those interested in literature and art, the largest group studying art history are art school students. These students of art history mostly cannot escape the two aforementioned fates. Ten years ago, the author saw students at the Shanghai Art College who would get headaches when they heard about [Art History] class or would doze off during lectures. This is an extremely unfortunate thing in the course of artistic movement. However, this misfortune does not come about by chance, but has various causes and consequences.

[Art] is a specialized discipline. [Art History] is even more specialized. If we want to study [Art History], we must first have some preparation. For example: (1) logical concepts, (2) the budding idea of beauty, (3) pure rational criticism, (4) knowledge of antiquities and anthropology, (5) opportunities to directly interact with works of art, etc.; all of these are things that people who study art history should have in advance.

Regarding the first point – logical concepts – we must have the [understanding] and [systematic concepts] of philosophy and science. At least we should have some familiarity with these two subjects.

Regarding the second point – the budding idea of beauty – this belongs to the realm of aesthetics, that is, those who study Western art history should at least have a general understanding of the recognition of beauty and the principles of beauty.

Regarding the third point – pure rational criticism – that is to say, those who study art history must have a rational certainty in their own minds as the basis for their art criticism.

Regarding the fourth point – antiquities and anthropology are the foundation of history. Art history is certainly no exception. Because to seek the lineage of an artistic trace, these disciplines are necessary knowledge to help him.

Regarding the fifth point – having the opportunity to directly contact works of art – this means that those who study art history can live in an artistic environment, with actual works of art in art museums and exhibitions for them to view and reference.

The above-mentioned aspects are no longer a problem in Western Europe, but in China, they are full of problems!

First, there are very few people who study the theory of beauty. And there are very few people who sincerely study it. So-called theoretical subjects like [aesthetics] are really a kind of [unpopular goods] that are most difficult to sell in Chinese society's marketplace. Therefore, in China, the [aesthetic consciousness] of art historians is extremely difficult to cultivate.

Secondly, China lacks an artistic environment such as [art museums] and [art exhibitions of famous people]. Moreover, there are not a large number of [works] to enrich [art museums] and [art exhibitions] to provide art historians with a kind of research and verification.

These important conditions for studying art history are either not available in China, or are superficially available, but not complete, which is truly the most unfortunate encounter for those studying art history.

In order to break through this situation and make it easier and more interesting for modern Chinese people to study art history, in addition to making the above-mentioned preparations, the methods of teaching art history or compiling art history must also be carefully chosen.

The most important things to pay attention to for those who teach or compile art history are:

(1) The mutual relationship between art in this era and that era.

(2) The causes and consequences of the formation of art, and its development.

(3) The characteristics of art in different eras and regions.

(4) The power of art and its relationship with humanity.

(5) Seeking the essence of [aesthetic consciousness] in the process of art development.

(6) Using the theory of beauty to evaluate the value of a certain art or a certain era's art in a certain region.

(7) Using the entity of works of art to explain the principles of aesthetics.

The above are the minimum requirements that I have for those who teach and compile art history.

On Mirror Lake 216

— Li Huiying

It was dusk, and the drizzling rain of June fell intermittently, covering the entire Mirror Lake in a layer of rain and mist.

This kind of rain is the most stifling, and for old man Wang, it is even more of a regret: Yellow croaker are only willing to swim to the surface on clear days, but now, they have all sunk to the bottom of the lake.

It seemed that the fishing work could not continue. While rowing the small boat, he collected the [silk nets] that were laid in the lake. After collecting them all, he saw that the fish in the basket were not even half full. After working for most of the day, he had only caught so few fish. A kind of unspeakable sadness penetrated into the depths of his heart, and he immediately sighed:

[Ah! This business, I'm afraid it's not for me.]

And in his practical experience, in recent years, especially recently, the fish seem to be not as plentiful as before. He did not understand why.

With a disappointed and sentimental mood, he rowed the small boat through the willow forest on the edge of the lake, letting the drizzle quietly beat his clothes, rowing straight towards the southeast corner. The oar stroked the lake water, making a flowery sound, constantly turning up some white foam. He was going home. His home was on the ground on the southeast edge of the lake, where an old partner was waiting for him to have dinner.

Thinking of dinner, he knew that there would be nothing satisfactory tonight. The fish from these few days could not be sold or transported out. The fish markets in several towns near the south and north ends of the lake, and Shitou Dianzi, could not sell anything. The people there were all fleeing chaotically to other places. It was said that in Ning'an and Dunhua, Japanese soldiers and righteous armies were fighting fiercely, and the Jingpo Lake area in the middle of these two places was bound to suffer from war. However, old man Wang did not appear flustered because of this. Over the years, he had viewed war very normally. Every summer, battles between soldiers and bandits were bound to happen near the lake, but none of them had affected old man Wang in any way. Until now, he was still working as a fisherman, living with his old partner by fishing.

At this time, the surface of the lake was even more heavily covered by mist. The range that old man Wang's eyes could see was only a small circle around him, but he had long been familiar with the path. Even in the darkest night, he could still row home with his eyes closed.

Several boats rowed past him from the opposite direction. In the dimness, he saw that the boats were loaded with things and crowded with people. The people seemed to have a flustered expression. By the time he wanted to take a closer look at who they were, those boats had already rowed past him and plunged into the thick mist. At the same time, he seemed to hear two loud [thump] [thump] sounds. He was stunned and thought:

[Is that the sound of artillery? Is the war coming?]

He had lived for more than fifty years, and had never really heard the sound of artillery, but in his consciousness, he guessed that only the sound of artillery could be so loud. He thought of the lonely old partner at home, so he hurriedly rowed the boat, rushing home to see how she was.

[Uncle Wang, run quickly, the Japanese soldiers are coming.]

Suddenly, he heard a familiar shout, coming from the surface of the lake, but he could not guess who it was for a moment. Looking around, it was Zhang Liuzi on a boat rowing past nearby who was shouting at him, so busy that he didn't even wait to finish his next sentence before rowing into the thick fog again, leaving him only with the chaotic sound of oars.

This unexpected change came unexpectedly. It seemed to be very serious. He understood that the few boats that had rowed past on the lake just now were escaping. So what should he do? He had an idea.

[There's nothing of value, what's there to be afraid of!]

Having made this decision, he continued to row the boat forward, only feeling that the boat was rowing too slowly. When he rowed to the Tu Kan place, he met his old partner, who was shouting loudly on the Kan, so that he could break through the fog and get her on the boat. The house at home was burned, the Japanese soldiers said because they were afraid of harboring righteous armies in the future. He was stunned after hearing what his old partner said. He had no idea what to do, and could only row the boat in the opposite direction, as if that way he could find a place to belong.

Random Notes from Qu Lu 217

— Zizhan

Qin devoured the six states, and the scholars of the six states hated Qin. I remember this as the starting line of Gu Yanwu's "Emperor Qin's Journey". In my humble opinion, those who hate Qin are not limited to the six states. It can even be said that Qin is the public enemy of scholars since annexing the six states. The articles cursing Qin that are still often recited by people today are Jia Yi's "The Faults of Qin" and Du Mu's "Ode to the Afang Palace", which are especially outstanding. I also recited these two articles when I was young. I once wrote a historical poem, one of which says:

What harm is there in trying to speak once?

Meeting on the Yi River opens up the path to hegemony.

Even the First Emperor's whip that moved the stone causes it to bleed,

Huangshi deliberately brings his hatred!

My teachers and friends praised it, but I didn't boast about it much, just kept the manuscript. As I grew older and read more books, I began to know that many good works by predecessors mentioned the affairs of Emperor Qin. I was most influenced by three quatrains, one by Zhang Jie about burning books and burying scholars:

The bamboo and silk texts are burned, the imperial dream gone,

The passes and rivers lock the First Emperor's abode in vain.

The ashes in the pits are not yet cold, and Shandong is in chaos,

Liu and Xiang, in the end, did not read books!

One by Chen Fuzhi about Bolangsha:

A bold spirit to strike the carriage,

The First Emperor's state was already shaken.

How is it that beyond the twelve bronze men,

There is still iron in the human world that has not been melted!

One by Chen Gongyin about reading the Annals of Qin:

Slander is easy to dispel, but resentment is hard to remove,

Qin's laws were strict, but also quite lax.

Calling for a child by the bridge in the middle of the night,

There are still books in the human world that have not been burned!

This poem "[there are still books in the human world that have not been burned]," and the previous poem "[there is still iron in the human world that has not been melted]" seem to share the same meaning, but they do not seem to be copying each other, because one praises burning books, and the other praises destroying weapons. A certain Mr. of the Beiyang Army, who was also quite capable of writing poetry, wrote a quatrain about burning books:

Whose argument from Jixia should be taken?

The First Emperor burned it all in a torch!

If we were to discuss the merits and demerits of burning books,

It would be worth half the effort of deleting books.

This poem somewhat overturns the case of burning books. If the First Emperor were resurrected, he would surely be delighted. He would surely treat such literati as Li Si did, and the pit for burying the living would certainly not be set up for them. Who said that in the era of the tyrannical Qin, all Confucian scholars were buried?

Two Brothers (7) (7) 218

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

[If it were possible, I would very much like to depart on this mail ship.]

Zhean asked him,

[Why can't you?]

[Because I don't know anyone at the Atlantic mail ship company.]

Luo Lan asked in surprise,

[And all your great plans for success? Have you abandoned them all?]

Bi'er said in a low voice,

[Sometimes we must know how to sacrifice everything, to abandon even the best hopes. And, this is just a beginning, a means of earning a few francs in preparation for starting my own business later.]

His father was immediately convinced by his words:

[That's right. In two years, you can save six or seven thousand francs, and if this money is used well, your future is limitless. What do you think, Louise?]

She replied in a low, almost inaudible voice:

[I think what Bi'er said makes sense.]

Luo Lan called out,

[But I'll go talk to Mr. Punan about this, I know him very well! He is a judge of the Commercial Court and he takes on matters for the ship company. I also know the shipowner, Mr. Le Yang, who is very close to a vice-chairman.]

Zhean asked his brother,

[Is it okay if I go sound out Mr. Ma Shang today?]

[Okay.]

Bi'er thought for a moment and then said,

[I'm afraid the best way would still be to write a letter to my professors at the medical university, they all value me very much. The doctors who go to these ships are usually mediocre characters. If Professors Maslosser, Le Miozo, Flasche, and Poligel write enthusiastic letters of introduction, it will definitely be more reliable and faster than all unreliable requests. All that is needed is for your friend, Mr. Ma Shang, to present this letter to the board of directors.]

Zhean fully agreed:

[Your idea is excellent, excellent!]

So he smiled, relieved, because he was convinced that it would succeed, and he almost felt satisfied, for he could not be worried for long.

[Are you going to write to them today?] he said.

[I'll write in a while, right away. I don't want to drink coffee this morning, I'm too nervous.]

He got up and went out.

Commentary

The Restless Epicenter 219

— Nanhai Shaou

The pain of unemployment and the competition for survival have always been unfolding incessantly, both at home and abroad, in ancient and modern times. Especially accompanied by the modern trend of sharp material enjoyment, all kinds of contradictions go to extremes; that kind of competition and unruly movement become more intense.

The successful people in the city, on the summit, in the ivory palace, in the gentle country, enjoy the heavenly life of happiness to the fullest. The unsuccessful people are eternally trapped in the downtrodden and impoverished lower class.

Therefore, those who carry guns use the unemployed and helpless peasants as a talisman for their leopard and tiger tents, trampling on the accumulated white bones of generals and soldiers to climb to heaven because of material desires. The comrades in literary attire who hold seven-inch writing brushes cling to the banners of the armed comrades, hitching a ride, shouting the slogan of [liberating the masses], following each other to dust off their hats and enter the palace.

By the time they enter the hall and chamber, they lose their footing in the crowded heavens and fall out of the sky. Waking up from a bewildered dream, seeing the desolation, dryness, and embarrassment of the mortal world, and reminiscing about the splendor and comfort of heavenly life, the fire of restless thoughts cannot be dismissed at any moment, and they finally reach out their ape arms, somersaulting and riding the auspicious clouds, coming for another round!

For these moments that seem so important, all kinds of patterns are churning like waves without stopping.

The [epicenter] is born from this point. How can this [epicenter] be brought to extinction? Please ask those who read the Spring and Autumn Annals!

Dai Jitao's Childhood 220

— Chun Liu

In Dai Jitao's autobiography, [My Reading Notes], we can roughly learn about his childhood life. Dai Jitao is undoubtedly from Wuxing, but he was born in Guanghan County, Sichuan. His family was very poor when he was young. He lost his grandfather at the age of six. His father was imprisoned in the ritual office of the state for two years because of disputes left by his grandfather. Jitao also attended on him in custody. At that time, he was only eleven years old. He studied very hard and had a high talent. He even listed grand books such as "Wenxian Tongkao" and "Fangyu Jiyao" as ancient prose courses. He lost his father at the age of thirteen. His brother ordered him to enter the Dongyou Preparatory School in Chengdu to prepare to learn Japanese well, and then go to Japan to study. At the age of fourteen, he transferred to the Chengdu Kejiji School, but was expelled for starting a student movement. At the age of fifteen, he became a Japanese translator in a middle school with the introduction of a Japanese, Xiao Ya Sanqi. His brother saw that he was very promising, so he sold thirty mu of sand fields in his home, earning seven hundred yuan, to pay for his study abroad in Japan. At that time, his grandmother was still alive and resolutely forbade him to travel far. As a result, the brothers colluded and let him run away secretly.

He studied in Japan for four years and returned to China at the age of nineteen, teaching in a specialized school in Suzhou. Later, with the introduction of Mr. Hong Foshe, he joined "Tianduo Newspaper" as editor-in-chief, which was the beginning of his life as a journalist. He was twenty-one years old at that time.

Street Sketches 221

— Bi Weng

In the center of Nanjing Road in Shanghai, there is a place with a long history called [Rising Sun Building]. Mentioning this name is truly known to both women and children. But this noisy Rising Sun Teahouse, somehow, transformed itself two years ago, becoming [Fanghu Wine Lodge], and soon became [Nanyue Restaurant]. Fortunately, after tea and wine, these are all matters of the states of Lu and Wei, and there is no need to get to the bottom of it. The worldwide recession has also affected our most prosperous Nanjing Road. The flags of big discounts are commonplace, and the tricks of big sales are endless. We often see a certain Hua Silk Shop with what [Clearance Sale]? What [Entrusted Consignment Sale by a Certain Factory in the Ninth District]? What [Shareholders Disagree, Implementing a Big Sacrifice?] All kinds of incoherent announcements are changing every day. Those who know the situation are secretly snickering; but they are simply unspeakably miserable! The rent is so expensive, and the staff cannot be cut any more. Expenses are necessary. The goods placed in the display window cannot be converted into gold yuan. If they don't come up with moving slogans like this, who would be willing to stop?

At any tram stop, there are beggars with their hands outstretched asking for copper coins, standing guard there; but in secret, they are all striking matches to smoke cigarettes, alas! Cigarettes are not food, they can't save this generation of beggars. They are simply pathetic and unworthy of pity. Sometimes, the detectives of the patrol house are disturbed, and a large prison van drives over, and they are all arrested, big and small, male and female, indiscriminately. At that time, if they resist a little bit, five cigars are awarded, the taste of which seems to be even better than cigarettes. I cannot make a judgement on this question.

We often see in foreign films that Chinese children are portrayed as being very skilled at playing with three small knives, up and down, catching three blades with both hands, very flexibly; this is the trick that little beggars use to beg for money from foreigners; foreigners have this deeply imprinted in their minds, and it represents the playthings of Chinese children; this is such a shameful and prejudiced thing! Speaking of the stubbornness of foreigners and their inability to understand the progress of the Chinese era, it can be seen everywhere, such as the paintings recently posted by the Public Works Department on trams or poles, warning Chinese children to get vaccinated quickly; the clothing and hats of the children are simply still before the Republic of China; and the greeting cards in Christmas gifts also have the clothing of my Chinese compatriots that are separated from the times by at least ten years.

Looking at Advertisements 222

— Shijiu

Newspapers are centered on news, but they cannot be separated from advertisements. Therefore, when we buy a newspaper, in addition to reading the news, we can also look at the colorful advertisements; and we may even buy cheap goods from the advertisements, or even make unexpected windfalls. As for which, news or advertisements, is more loved by people, although it seems not easy to determine: there are also traces to be found. In short, in a country in times of peace, the advertisements on newspapers are always more than the news; conversely, the news is always more than the advertisements. Therefore, the rise and fall of a country's fortune can be easily followed by this track. This is the experience I have gained from reading newspapers for decades. If I want to give an example, I can briefly describe it as follows:

In the year of Xinhai, the Wuchang Uprising broke out. The newspapers were full of articles competing to publish the news that a certain province was independent and that someone had revolted, which made people's eyebrows dance when they read it. Therefore, people who care about national affairs all want to compete to read the news as soon as they get the newspaper. As for advertisements, except for [foreign currency exchange rates] which are worth paying attention to by those who care about finance, the rest, 8

At that time, he had to let the news take the lead alone.

Also, in the year when the [January 28th] incident occurred, I was trapped in a certain rear area. One day, I went to the YMCA and saw thousands of people crowded together, some of whom were still mumbling in their mouths. It turned out that a Shanghai newspaper was stuck on the wall. This newspaper was brought back from the front line. At that time, everyone cared about the news from the front line; I think even if the newspaper was full of eye-catching 8

Advertisements, I am afraid that no one would pay attention to them.

From the above two examples, it can be proved that when the country is in trouble, the people value news and ignore advertisements. Conversely, the domain of news in newspapers is gradually occupied by advertisements, which may be a sign of peace in the world. Therefore, we don't need to sigh [nothing to see], nor do we need to hold the heart of [worrying about the sky falling], it is better to look at the advertisements more, and when we encounter something we love, whether it is for eating or using, we might as well buy more. You must know how many lives there are, why bother yourself? Knowing this is worthy of reading the newspaper, worthy of reading the advertisements on the newspaper.

Random Notes from the West Window 223

— An Fu

Curves on a woman's body originally have time-based differences. The breasts and buttocks of a young girl are beautiful; the wrinkles on an old lady's forehead, although they are also curves, are ugly.

Why do women like to dress up? If you remove the saying that women are born with a love of beauty; if you study further, you will definitely get a mysterious answer.

A woman who works in an office has a monthly salary of forty yuan, and the monthly cost of makeup is also forty yuan, but she herself says that she is still the most frugal.

A woman who is tired of socializing said: Arranged by parents, marrying a man she doesn't know; it may be better than a man she is already familiar with. Because their friendship and love happened at the same time.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 224

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 21: Whispered Words by the Lamp, Heartfelt Advice to the Weak Child / Leaning on a Staff, Watching Heroes with Cold Eyes Down the Mountain

Guizhi was listening in bed and couldn't bear it anymore. She sat up with a flip, pushed her half-untidy hair to her cheeks, and said with a straight face: Look at you, old man, the more you talk, the more unpleasant it becomes. What indecent thing did I do! It won't work, don't shout too much, from tomorrow onwards, I am determined not to take a step out of the gate. If I step out of the gate, I will not die a good death in this life. There are several bottles of floral water, snow cream jars, etc. by the pit. Guizhi picked up one at hand and smashed it on the ground with a snap. Pointing to the ground, she said: If I don't mean what I say, I'll be like this bottle. Ms. Jiang thought that her daughter had received a lesson and was quite proud of herself. She had a belly full of words to be vented and wanted to take this opportunity to say them all. Unexpectedly, the girl suddenly resisted so violently that it made her stop speaking, but it was not good, and it was also not good to continue speaking. So she blushed, stood up and looked at Guizhi and said: What do you mean by this? When you get married, you will soon be an adult. Can you be so unreasonable to your superiors? When you get older in the future, will you be able to accept it if your subordinates treat you like this? Guizhi said: I didn't say that your words were bad. 8

Because your words are right, and I am afraid that you will not worry about me, so I smashed this perfume bottle to show that I have made up my mind. Ms. Jiang stood under the lamp, her face red and white with anger, but since the girl had lost her temper, she was afraid that she would shout if she continued to talk to her, which would be even more inconvenient. She put her hands behind her back and supported the table, sneering: Look, this half-head is rebellious. Guizhi shook her head slightly and said: Not rebellious at all, I am telling the truth. Ms. Jiang saw that the girl's attitude was still so stubborn, and wanted to say two more sentences. But she heard Zhao Weng coughing several times in the back yard. (284)

Gold Market Continues to Plunge 228

丨Market Shows Signs of Drying Up丨

丨A Drop of $11.60丨

Although the gold market declined yesterday, the day's market conditions were still obscure. In reality, while there were many sellers, a significant portion was largely hedging exchange bills, which provided substantial support. This led to more active bargain hunting, and the market showed slight signs of drying up, resulting in a stable situation. At the beginning of the morning, although overseas silver markets in the UK and US both declined, the forward silver price on the Gold Exchange actually rose by 0.04 to 0.045, and exchange rates also increased. The pure gold price remained unchanged, but US cotton rose by more than a point per pound, and US wheat also increased. Stocks declined slightly. Wool futures opened lower but remained above $80. Subsequently, due to slightly worse news from foreign telegrams, they fell further. After the opening, although Reuters had a message about US Senators King and Wheeler proposing free coinage of silver, the telegram ended with a message that after Senator Rubin spoke with the President, he told people that this bill might not be introduced in the current Congress. Although it declined, it remained stable. Subsequently, due to the US dollar exchange rate rising and rumors worsening, it fell, but banks had a good appetite, hedging activities stabilized the market, and the after-market was even stronger. The day's market conditions were mediocre, with the spot price being $1055. Now, the day's market conditions are recorded as follows:

The morning opened at $675, down $12.40 from the previous close. Goods opened at $5.50.
