Financial Market Conditions Gradually Weakening 231

丨Various Business Transactions Gradually Ending丨

Shanghai's financial industry has always had the custom of treating the period after the National Lunar New Year holiday as the deadline for the year's major conclusion, in order to finalize the year-end accounting by the end of January. This year's period has arrived, and various business transactions and outstanding debts must be concluded once again. Therefore, most current transactions are related to settling accounts, and new transactions are rarely seen. The interbank lending rate in the market remains at 7%, both morning and afternoon, with "cutting heads" at no more than 2-3% plus water, similar to the previous day. The transaction volume of discounted bills was 4.3 to 4.4 million in the morning transfer, and more than 500,000 in new transactions and afternoon transactions. Silk and Tea, Silk Cocoon Merchants Plan to Establish an Exchange 246

▲ Overseas Silk Still Has No Turning Point

(Silk Cocoon Exchange Actively Being Organized) With the sluggish sales of Xianmei silk, the sericulture industry in our country is on the verge of total collapse. At the end of last year, the silk factories' trade associations of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces held a joint meeting in Shanghai and decided to organize a silk cocoon exchange to seek a way to save the industry. Yesterday, when interviewed, Mr. Shen Huachen, chairman of the Shanghai Silk Factories' Trade Association, said that the matter of the silk cocoon exchange is now being handled by a committee including Zhou Qianchu, who is drafting the articles of association, and Chen Zezhong, Zhang Yunsheng, and Chen Bingruo, who are reviewing them. The planned capital is 250,000 yuan. Once the drafting is completed, another meeting will be held to discuss and prepare, and then it will be submitted to the Ministry of Industry for registration. From this, it can be seen that the opening date should not be far off.

(Over a Hundred Pieces of Silk Waste Shipped to Mumbai) This time, the British mail ships Bengal No. 1 and No. 2 exported a total of 125 pieces of long silk cocoons and silk waste, owned by Anli and others, destined for Mumbai.

(Futures Sales of Artificial Silk Gradually Rising in Spring) Since the New Year, inland merchants' appetite for artificial silk futures has gradually increased. Yesterday, merchants from Yantai and other places bought 34 cases of Jin Qilin, Black Beauty, and Flying Elephant brands, weighing one hundred pounds per case, for January and February delivery, at prices ranging from 198 yuan, 2 jiao, 5 fen to 184 yuan, 7 jiao, 5 fen net (goods numbered 80 to 200).

(Sales of Coarse Silk for Printing Remain Flat and Weak) In the overseas raw silk market, after the New Year's opening, the silk shops' appetite remains sluggish. Warehouses still have ample silk inventory. The opening price of Japanese silk in New York is difficult to increase, and actual sales in Lyon have not picked up, so prices remain low. Sales of European and American silk still lack any turning point. The market atmosphere in Shanghai remains weak, and few silk telegrams are being sent. Yesterday, only printing houses bought 11 packages of yellow and white silk, with the red market price remaining flat and weak.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Rambling Remarks

This Year's Women and Children 261

— Li Zhai

Because this year is [Women's National Products Year] and [Children's Year], therefore [women], who have always been despised by some moralists, and [children], who have been ignored by many people, have actually [climbed to the peak of the times] and become objects that people often mention or write about.

Fairly speaking, who dares to say that women should not use national products? Who also says that the happiness of children should not be valued? However, in our complex and turbulent country, where beautiful arguments are often slapped in the face by facts with [cigars], these are all [major problems]!

First, let's talk about women and national products: The [patriotic people] have been using [national products to save the country] to replace [resisting Japan] for two years now. But in the actual situation, we still only see the [daily decline] of national industries, the overwhelming import of Japanese goods, and the [way to make money] of many traitors. This iron-like fact is enough to prove that the wealthy and profit-seeking class of Chinese society has long been dead at heart and its blood is cold. The [life philosophy] of the group of traitors is simply [ancestral graves can be dug up, but Japanese goods cannot be sold]! Therefore, last year's [National Products Year], which was very vigorous, did not turn out to be [good and wonderful]. Now, the [equal rights for men and women] of [National Products Year] is split into [Women's National Products Year], so what will be the future result? Alas! If I say it bluntly, it will inevitably [spoil people's fun]; if I don't say it, it will be somewhat [like a fishbone in my throat]! First, the daily necessities, especially luxury goods, of foreigners are both expensive and [good], and have long become an [indispensable] [life element] for women in the upper class of Chinese society, who take pleasure and indulgence as their principle! Now, to promote [Women's National Products Year], in fact, those noble ladies and celebrities will inevitably be [excluded] and cannot be counted on. Second, because of the dumping of foreign goods with good quality and low prices, and the exploitation of national products with numerous checkpoints, the daily necessities of the middle and lower classes are actually mostly more expensive for national products than foreign goods. Therefore, to require poor women who are on the verge of bankruptcy and whose purchasing power is extremely weak to [use national products only] for the sake of [patriotism], which they don't quite understand, seems impractical. As a result, [Women's National Products Year] cannot but be truncated, targeting a part of the petty-bourgeois women who are slightly knowledgeable and can afford national products. Therefore, I am afraid that not many [national industrialists] will be created from [Women's National Products Year]? At the same time, the number of imported goods will not necessarily be slightly reduced because of the loud call of [Women's National Products Year]? However, I still hope that my prediction is [wrong]!

Secondly, let's talk about [Children's Year]: Now, it is a disastrous era of universal bankruptcy, with most people falling into the path of hungry ghosts. Among the 400 million people, at least 350 million people's children are trapped in the hellish life of insufficient food and clothing, starvation, scavenging garbage, pulling rickshaws, and being maids and prostitutes. Therefore, in fact, most of China's children have become [semi-beggars]. The [interests] of these children, unless China's politics and people's livelihood have a way out, will never be guaranteed. Now, I think that the most practical task for enthusiastic [child care] volunteers is not how to sing loudly about [Children's Year], but to run a few more civilian day and night schools, prohibit the abuse and sale of children, and find some [drop in the bucket] relief for unfortunate children who are out of school and starving. Being able to do these things is already a great act of [merit for countless generations of nobles and marquises], who would dare to expect so much from [Children's Year]! As for those [children's paradises] displayed in major companies and the [scientific] food, clothing, housing, and transportation of children, which are calculated in dollars, they are just to find a little more fun for the [little darlings] of the rich. In fact, these [darlings] have long been wanted by their parents to be held in their mouths, and even without promoting [Children's Year], they are already happy to the [special first class], why would they need volunteers to brag about it in such a serious way!

What I have seen in [Women's National Products Year] and [Children's Year] is just [that's all]!

Shadows on the Dry Bridge 262

— Old Brand

For four full months, I had to cross this dry bridge twice a day on time.

The reputation of the job of begging for a living was not bad, but the salary was so low that it made people ashamed, and the agency was located in the most affluent area, where it was simply impossible to solve the problem of food and accommodation. The fact forced me to live far away in the home of a fellow villager in North Shanghai, and run back and forth on time every day, crossing this dry bridge twice a day on time.

Originally, I should have crossed it four times, but because my legs were too sore from running, and two blisters the size of silver dollars appeared on the soles of my feet, I changed my mind, preferring to endure one hunger in the middle of the day, saving two trips. At about nine o'clock every morning, after eating a meal that was neither early nor late, I set off to do the [immovable] official business. It took about half an hour to run on the dirty road to reach the foot of the dry bridge, which naturally provided an opportunity to [rest a little]. Alas, the people crossing the bridge were so crowded! The warm sun slowly rose high from the east, calling up the coolies, rickshaw pullers, laborers, vendors, and all kinds of other coolies in the stacked slums of North Shanghai, carrying various tools, gathered on the narrow roads leading to the foot of the bridge, layer by layer close to each other. When they reached the section near the foot of the bridge, they became in a situation of [buttocks touching buttocks and heads bumping heads]. When time was running out, I was one of the members of this situation. Since people were so crowded, everyone wanted to squeeze past first, but the fact just didn't allow it. After a while of chaos, first, a string of [national curses] was practiced: [Mom's] [dog's X] from Jiangbei people, [X your mother's X] from Shandong guys, [X your mother] from Guangdong oldies, [Mom selling X's] from Hunan people, [X your sister] from Hubei buddies; if it was more fierce, people would roll down from the bridge to the foot of the bridge one by one. Then [cursing] stopped abruptly, and only the sound of punching and kicking was heard, as chaotic as boiling smoke, and traffic was virtually cut off, so that everyone could not cross over.

When I encountered this kind of occasion, I had to avoid the road, took a big circle, and detoured from the railway station side, and I could still vaguely see that it was so chaotic, as if they were sworn enemies, with no end to the quarrel.

However, this was not the case every day. On some days, everyone was particularly polite, almost to the point of [using force], but after all, they passed peacefully by accident. Then there were two stereotyped sentences that came out of everyone's mouth one by one, which were: [We are all family, let's just muddle through!]. The crowded people walked past one by one in this crowded sound.

On a certain day, I went a little late. When I stepped onto the top of the bridge, I saw a group of vendors picking up their scattered belongings with tearful faces. I asked them what was the reason, whether they had been kicked over by the police. They said: [No, the police don't come at this time. Originally, we could freely peddle on this bridge, but we encountered a group of people crossing the bridge who fought for the lead, knocking over all our belongings, and everyone ran away.] [Oh, so that's it. There was another riot this morning!] This impression will never be forgotten by me! Every morning when I passed there, I not only became wary myself, but also worried a lot about those vendors.

At night, at about ten o'clock late at night, I crossed this dry bridge again with a tired and hungry body. However, at this time, it was much quieter, also because I was eager to rush back to eat, and rarely paid attention to the people around me. Under the bleak electric torch, everything presented a dim sense of gloom and panic. On the top of the bridge, occasionally one or two vendors were calling out to sell in a halting voice, and more were barefoot blind people and all kinds of other compatriots who were begging for food, arranging their sleep

Page 20

equipment, arranging them side by side, one after another. Also, there were always two or three fellow countrymen who were so leisurely, leaning on the bridge railing in neat clothes, whispering to each other, as if they were shouldering some kind of mission, and were waiting for something. That was probably the gentlemen of the Shanghai night, I thought.

I noticed very carefully that very few Western-dressed people crossed this dry bridge, and even fewer modern girls. However, it gave me a very deep impression, and its relationship with me was very close! Hastily, I haven't crossed it for a year, but it is forever and ever engraved in my heart.

Newspapers and Textbooks 263

— Qu Chen

Knowing that newspapers are a kind of textbook is a major improvement I have made recently.

In the past, I always believed that newspapers represented public opinion and reported news. Now I know that this is not the case. Some news is produced in order to be reported. And what is called public opinion...... Although the sign is this one, it always seems a bit boring.

I remember that I once saw in a joke book (probably Shi Tianji's "Laugh Well") a story about a fool reading a book, and after looking at it carefully for three days, he realized that the words on the book were printed, not written. At that time, I laughed at it. Unexpectedly, I have been reading newspapers for more than ten years, and only today did I realize that newspapers are also a kind of textbook. So I deeply regret that I laughed too early.

Modern newspapers are clearly divided into two classes: one is those who compile the newspapers, and the other is those who read the newspapers. Those who compile the newspapers are obviously in the position of teachers, while those who read the newspapers are like primary school students who have been assigned, and the newspapers are equivalent to textbooks between teachers and students.

The teacher says: You should respect the teacher. You should do as the teacher teaches you. You must not resist the teacher's orders. So he added a lesson to the textbook. If there are really a few students who do not obey the teacher's orders, or reveal the teacher's shortcomings, then the teacher says: You have violated the school rules and are given a major demerit. So he wrote another lesson in the textbook for you to read. In fact, although the demerit is recorded, the naughty students always refuse to repent and change their ways, but the teacher always thinks it is very appropriate in front of everyone. Otherwise, if the teacher beat the students, how could this lesson be taught? People are so good at thinking for the sake of reading!

Textbooks teach people the knowledge they should learn, such as those who study chemistry, know that two parts hydrogen and one part oxygen equals water. The mission of learning newspapers is to let you know the same. I dare not say that it is because the teacher is not good and I do not understand. I always blame myself for being too stupid and not being able to understand. Therefore, students who read books to death often become bookworms, while smart students will draw inferences from one instance and understand similar things. No matter what the teacher does, the students' knowledge will naturally advance.

— Recent works by Ms. Ming Yong, granddaughter of Mr. Li Junong, the former governor of Zhejiang (the lady is a native of Wuxian County, Jiangsu)

*** Road in 1933 265

— Bin Fu

The 365 days of 1933 have passed in an unknown way. Taking advantage of the opportunity at the beginning of the new year, if we make a general reckoning of the events we have experienced in the most recent 365 days, it may not be without significance.

The ancients said, "Forget the family for the country, forget the private for the public." Based on this ancient训, we should naturally put our national affairs on the first page of the general reckoning table, and should not mention our personal trivial family affairs. Therefore, I have set the title of this article as: "China in the Past Year."

The title is set, but the difficulty arises: Is such a broad topic for a big article suitable for a young guy like me to write?

So I narrowed the title to "Shanghai in the Past Year."

Although this topic is much smaller than the previous one

Page 21

many, however, the various aspects of the ten-mile foreign field cannot be fully described by the [talented people] who roam in it. As for me, who crouches in a corner all day long, to give a longitudinal narrative of the vast Shanghai in the past year, the result can only be a [frog in a well] ridicule. Therefore, I have to find a way to change the title again.

To be honest, since the New Year's Day of 1933 until today, I have not left Shanghai for more than half a month. Except for fifty-two Sundays and occasional holidays, I go to work from my residence to the office every day, leaving early and returning late, living an extremely mechanical life every day. In this way, I am naturally separated from the [outside world]. The only thing I am more familiar with is the XXX Road that I had to pass through from my residence to the office last year. Since XXX Road is a corner of Shanghai society, why not find this corner of society as the subject matter? Therefore, the title of this article was finally finalized: [XXX Road in 1933]

XXX Road is a very long road on the most remote west side of the French Concession. Its length is no less than Jing'an Temple Road in the Public Concession. The difference is that it is not as wide and bustling as Jing'an Temple Road, but it is much quieter than Jing'an Temple Road.

At a certain point on this road, there is a barracks where foreign soldiers are stationed. Next to the barracks, there is a shooting range. Every morning, the shooting range makes a creaking sound, often startling the roosting birds in the woods. And I, too, am quite blessed by this [creaking] sound, so that I will not lose sleep and delay my work. The gate of the barracks is often lined with rickshaws. Each rickshaw puller stares at the gate of the barracks with [expectant] eyes. I think no one who enters or exits there will be missed by their gaze.

"Hallo 'licker'?" When one or a group of tall foreign soldiers in uniform come out of this gate, a group of [coolies] pull their rickshaws and rush over as fast as they can, like snatching food.

Sometimes, people in uniform like to take cars. Sometimes, they like to walk. The [coolies] then look at each other and smile bitterly. Sometimes, people in uniform wave their hands and get into the car, and the coolies feel blessed and run away as fast as they can. Sometimes, people in uniform have excessive anger or joy in their hearts, so they beat the faces or backs of the [coolies] to vent their anger. The coolies? Then they put their sleeves with rags to defend themselves, but their faces always had a smile.

There is a very large square on XXX Road. Football fans will think that this is really suitable for a football field when they see it. However, now, it is piled with stones and overgrown with green grass. From New Year's Day to New Year's Eve, whether it is morning or night, you can see three or two workers or rickshaw pullers squatting there to excrete, often causing modern men and women to avoid it. As time goes by, a lot of excrement accumulates. If a strong wind blows, [toilet paper] will inevitably fly and the fragrance will spread everywhere. From this, we can understand that for the working masses living in the city, even excretion is a serious problem.

Walking on XXX Road, you can see a very magnificent dog mansion. There are probably seventy or eighty dogs there. They have more than a dozen servants to serve them. They eat bread, they wear brocade, and they sleep on thick velvet. Which of us working people has their comfort? However, they can run after electric rabbits in Yiyuan every Saturday, and we cannot. Then, it is only natural that they are given special preferential treatment.

What I know of XXX Road in 1933 is just these. As for the wife's car running over people, the vegetable seller being beaten, etc., these trivial matters do not need to be recorded, and I cannot remember so many. In short, after reading the above fragmented facts, do readers feel that this seems to be a reflection of the entire Chinese society?

The Most Profitable Nation 266

— Bai Tao

[Everything goes wrong when it comes to China!] A friend who had just returned from abroad said, [Look, people use radio to transmit news and make public academic speeches. But when it comes to China, Chinese people use it to broadcast Tanhuang and ditties. The streets and alleys are full of vulgar Bangzi tunes, which are really noisy!]

This is naturally true. No matter what good things, they go wrong when they come into the hands of Chinese people. Take opium, for example. Foreigners use it to treat diseases, but when it comes to China, smart Chinese people put it on opium pipes to smoke. This is bad. Once you get addicted, unless you are a millionaire, you will end up bankrupting your family.

Some people say: Chinese people only know how to enjoy, not how to create. This is naturally also true. Foreigners make guns and cannons for themselves to play with. But Chinese people want to buy ready-made ones from foreigners. Take airplanes, for example. There are quite a few that are bought from the United States alone. Americans make airplanes and ship them to China one ship after another. After the Chinese people arrive at their homes, they still have to wait for them to assemble everything properly. After the assembly is done, they have to wait for him to sit on it and play with it once for themselves to see before they can take it down.

To give another example, such as cars. There are many Chinese people who take cars. Everyone takes pride in taking a car. People who have a little money want to buy a car. Moreover, in recent years, the government has been promoting the construction of highways, holding aviation road construction conferences, and issuing aviation road lottery tickets. People all over the country are enthusiastically contributing. Naturally, once the highway is built, even people who cannot afford to buy their own cars can take long-distance buses. Anyway, everyone has a car to ride. However, the cars they ride in are all bought ready-made from others. Chinese people simply do not want to make their own cars to ride in.

Fortunately, Chinese people are lucky. Many foreign brats are working hard to create! As long as my father has money, which foreign brat will not come to pay his respects to me!

A German silly boy saw it very clearly, perhaps because he had lived in China for a long time. One day, he said to several Chinese friends: [Yes, yes, what Chinese people want is things that others have made ready-made. The books that students read in Chinese schools are also the results of research by others. Chinese people are the most profitable nation in the world!]

Acknowledgements I would like to thank the Shen Bao Circulation Library for donating a [One-Week Commemorative Album] and the Lloyd Road Xi Shintai Hospital in the British Concession for donating two bottles of [Smooth] products, and the Information Section of the Aviation Administration for donating a booklet of aviation series [Glorious Battle]. I hereby express my thanks.

Novel

Prison Diary (2) 267

— Cartwheel

It's truly strange. In my dreams, I constantly ask myself, "Is this a dream?" I try all sorts of methods to prove whether it is a dream. I often think I've really gone home, really gotten out—because I have such vivid dreams. Once, I was discussing idealism versus materialism with Lao Sun. As we were walking together in a park, I asked him, "Are we not dreaming?" He said, "If it is a dream, then this is a victory for idealism." Yes, it is indeed a dream.

8th

On the 7th, Wu Mei and three classmates came to visit me. Those three didn't say a single word. What could be done?

Receiving a visitor is both a joyous and a painful thing. Before you can even finish three sentences, the voice urging you to leave cuts off your conversation. You have to beg him to extend the time a little. Although the rules stipulate half an hour, twenty minutes, or ten minutes, the prisoners aren't clear on this. In short, there is a rule; however, the person who truly decides the length of the visit is the warden who escorts us to the meeting—we call every guard "warden." If he is happy, it will be longer; if he is unhappy, it will be shorter. If a prisoner insists on a reasonable extension according to the rules, the prisoner will suffer. One can only plead with furrowed brows, in which case it might be extended by a minute or two, with ten minutes being the longest.

After he interrupts our conversation and we ask him to extend it, we waste some time. Then, when we want to continue our conversation, there's no way to continue, even though we have countless words we want to say. But just as you quietly try to resume the talk, that dog barks again.

Being without visitors is bearable, but having visitors and not being able to talk is the greatest pain for prisoners. So, prisoners are usually calm, but after a visit, they often cry, stare blankly, or become angry.

"Three hundred and ninety-three!"

As soon as I hear this number, I know it's the warden who escorts visitors. I also know right away that it's my sister coming, because no one else comes to visit me.

I had already packed up several cotton clothes, waiting for her to come and take them. At this time, I took them out and walked out. The head guard at the central post stopped me for inspection, suspecting that I might be carrying some small notes out, but I really hadn't cheated. Committing a minor offense—a useless offense—and adding to the lawsuit is really not worth it.

The area in front of the central observation platform is not usually walked by people having visitors, but my sister ignored their interference and came in. I handed her the bag of clothes directly—"Take it to the section for inspection!" the visiting warden told her. I said, "It's already been inspected at the central post!" She didn't take it for inspection later. Normally, you can't directly hand things to the person you want to give them to.

When handing over the clothes, I reached out to shake her hand. She looked at me as if she didn't understand, but immediately understood and squeezed my hand tightly, because this handshake was not a habitual action for her. She also knew this was a rare opportunity.

Indeed, standing together without obstruction in this situation is an extremely precious opportunity. In the visiting area, there are two layers of wooden fences and a layer of barbed wire separating visitors and prisoners, and you have to talk from several feet away. There's really no chance to shake hands. This was the first handshake between my sister and me. There was an opportunity before, and I wasn't separated from her by anything, but I didn't shake her hand. Honestly, I wanted to hug her, but I didn't even shake her hand. Looking back, I feel it was wrong and unreasonable to let go of this opportunity to show some affection—because we were too far apart, and we both desperately needed comfort!

Last time was because Zhao worked in the section, and I was allowed to talk to Zhao, and my sister was there too.

After handing the clothes to my sister, she was walking with me, and a guard, under the guise of checking the clothes, wanted to touch her breast—I can't forget this scene.

Page 22

Page 23

Film Special

Hollywood's Outlook for 1934 268

— Xifu

According to general speculation in Hollywood, this year will be an exceptionally hot year. The biggest reason is that the hottest star, Mae West, achieved unprecedented success last year, forcing other stars, who are still recovering their energy, to emulate her; otherwise, it will be difficult to get the audience's money flowing out of their pockets.

However, one thing to note is how "sex" will be portrayed on the screen in 1934. Everyone is hesitant to discuss this issue openly. Why? Because they are afraid that too much discussion will attract the attention of moralistic censors and cause complications. In addition, there are also social reformers. They take social improvement as their mission. Whenever a film has some "immoral" performances, they blush, clench their fists, and speak out. However, it is said that these people have recently become less vocal, partly because public opinion clashes too much with their views, and they are outmatched and change direction accordingly; partly because the film market is so sluggish that it needs hot, stimulating things to revitalize it. Social reformers, for the sake of the overall situation, cannot be too insistent on their own views. Even the film censorship board is quite understanding of the difficulties of the business and refrains from destructive actions. Therefore, works like Mae West's, which previously had little hope of passing, actually passed one by one in 1933. Even so, for the sake of caution, it is of course better to discuss less and produce more.

1934 will not only be hotter than before, but also add some nude scenes. American filmmakers have already been influenced by Russian and German films. Moreover, people are becoming more sophisticated year by year. Things that seemed novel in the past are now commonplace, and new and novel scenes must be sought. Therefore, the works of 1934 will definitely be hotter and more interesting than before, and the expression of human beauty will definitely be bolder.

In 1933, Mae West already set a precedent. In 1934, the following stars are said to be following suit: Pert Kelton, Ginger Rogers. There are also several who are not naturally inclined to romance, but because of their versatility, they are also preparing to change their style in 1934 and join the ranks of romantic stars. They are Helen Hayes, Kay Francis, Claudette Colbert, etc. They already tried their hand last year and unexpectedly reaped rewards.

Audiences are gradually becoming tired of movies for various reasons. Mae West is a hero of Hollywood's revival. Her emergence revitalized the industry. Ginger Rogers followed suit, stirring up a wave of heat in "Professional Sweetheart." Pert Kelton went even further, sacrificing her sexuality in "Bed of Roses" and winning great applause in 1934. Even Diana Wynyard, as gentle as a virgin, cannot help but cast flirtatious glances and exude seductive charm.

Film Review

Review of "Flames of Youth" 269

— Ling He

丨Tianyi Production · Carlton Screening丨

(1) Regarding Mr. Qiu Qixiang, we must not ignore his existence in Chinese cinema.

From "Lan Gu Ping Zong" and "Pursuit" to the recently released "Struggle," it is not difficult to find traces of his gradual progress in creative techniques. However, the ideology expressed in his works is somewhat elusive. "Lan Gu Ping Zong" or "Pursuit" shows us a tasteless love entanglement. By "Struggle," he seems to be positively showing a new tendency. Although it still preaches the doctrine of loyalty and forbearance, it does depict the suffering of farmers in the countryside. This makes us look forward to the bright future of Chinese cinema. However, people's minds are indeed mysteriously elusive!

(2) "Flames of Youth" is also written and directed by the author, which shows his complete control from the selection of material to the techniques of expression.

The characters in "Flames of Youth" are all lords, ladies, young ladies, and young masters in the military. Among these people, the author has created a Romanlism romance.

Of course, we do not ignore that the author has exposed the ugliness of officialdom, the nepotism among military officers, the private bestowal of ranks and titles. These all make us believe that this is a bold style. However, the theme of the story is not here; on the contrary, the sole purpose is the conclusion of the sacredness of love. Therefore, we cannot obtain considerable satisfaction from "Flames of Youth," especially when this love game has already been rejected by audiences in theaters.

Opposition to marriages arranged by parents and matchmakers seems to be a thing of the past. No matter why Liu Duban wants to marry his daughter to the brigade commander, no matter why Liu Duban wants to promote the brigade commander to division commander simply because he dotes on his daughter, and no matter that the beautiful daughter marries an ugly husband, we see that the author deeply sympathizes with and pities her, but the author has no way to make her escape her husband's embrace. Even Meng Xilian won't give her "a part of love," so she can only "sacrifice for love," ending her own life with a pistol and dying in the arms of her lover. Death is the explosion of the flames of youth, and the so-called pure love receives the author's great praise!

(4) I remember that in answering an interviewer's questions, Mr. Qiu once said that he was very saddened by the Americanization of Chinese film works. But until now, until this "Flames of Youth," Mr. Qiu's scripts and performances are all imitations of American films. Therefore, American films have deeply planted their roots in China, and here is another example.

(5) As mentioned above, the director's composition of the screen is indeed very pure and hot in some places. The smoothness of the editing and the appropriateness of the scenery are all strengths. However, the excessive number of unnecessary subtitles is a major flaw.

The most unsatisfactory aspect is the melodramatic acting of some actors, and the inappropriate insertion of gags, which is the director's responsibility. However, the most commendable aspect is the beauty of the scenery. Except for some Fade locations that are not very clear, the matching of lights is indeed worthy of praise!

Salt Tide Review 270

— Moore

Just like rice and even air, salt is something that almost everyone needs every day. On the shores of the Yellow Sea and the East Sea, there are millions, even tens of millions, of people who depend on it for survival; in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River, there are tens of millions, even hundreds of millions, of people who value it more than rice because it is difficult to obtain. But those who cannot obtain salt are indeed struggling to make a living due to other reasons, while those who make salt by hand are struggling to make a living even more, even to the point of starving and freezing to death. Thus, this boundless salt tide roared!

The sea is nature's inexhaustible treasure, but the salt produced must be exploited by salt merchants. The public wasteland where salt-burning bushes grow is formed by the rising of the sea, but after boundary markers are erected, it becomes the private property of powerful people. Burning salt without a license is "private burning," and you will be taken to the official; selling to salt peddlers who offer slightly higher prices instead of selling to salt merchants is "private peddling," and you will be taken to the official. When there is no rice and your mother is sick, five yuan worth of salt brine can only buy four, and thus the boundless salt tide roared!

Relying on one's special position and superior economy, setting traps to change the will of young girls and taking away other people's lovers—thus the boundless salt tide roared!

"The revolution is about to begin,

The people have risen..." (Song of the Iron Current)

In the boundless, roaring "Salt Tide," we hear such songs! Whether it is the warlord era of 1925, the present of 1934, or even the future after 1934, if the above-mentioned situation exists, this boundless "Salt Tide" will roar no matter what. "Local tyrants and evil gentry will eventually be overthrown" (general meaning of the subtitles). Naturally, it is the power of the masses themselves that overthrows them, not any other irrelevant "ism." In "Salt Tide," we see this clearly.

Naturally, the masses in "Salt Tide" are not heroes arbitrarily created by the writer. It seems that A'feng (played by Hu Die) is a young girl who can be tempted by the material possessions of Mr. Hu (played by Sun Min). She wants to go to Shanghai with Mr. Hu, but when she learns that Mr. Hu has enclosed the common salt bush land of their entire village, she becomes the most vehement resister. This is her class consciousness. Everyone wants to live better, but when they realize that their group is about to starve to death or encounter a major hardship, they will definitely unite with their group. The deception of the peasants-turned-workers in the film "Gold Mountain" finally awakens at the start of a great struggle; although salt workers are a little different from ordinary farmers, they "have land and houses" (Zhang Desan's words in the play) and are the same as ordinary farmers. Then, under this condition, A'feng's character and consciousness, as expressed in "Salt Tide," are absolutely correct. I remember a miner in "Destruction" saying: "No matter who it is, if you dig deeper and deeper, there will always be a farmer in their soul." (general meaning) "Because the city is in the embrace of the countryside, and the miners are intertwined with the farmers," let alone the daughter of a salt worker? As for Chen Bingsheng's (played by Wang Zhengxin) firmer stance, it is also inevitable. Don't you see his conditions of "private peddling" and "youth"? The future world is created by youth!

Written Before the Premiere of "Flames of Youth" 271

— Cang Bo

"Youth": What a lovely, beautiful word. "Flame" is also such an exciting, passionate thing, let alone this "Flame" is the "Flame of Youth"? Ah! This flame is too passionate.

Every man and woman in the world, who doesn't want to keep his or her youth forever, who isn't burning with this flame of youth, whether male or female, ugly or beautiful, who isn't intoxicated by this lovely flame, even though this flame may sometimes scorch your skin, or even burn your heart? But they still move forward bravely and rush headlong into this lovely flame, some returning in triumph, others retreating with serious injuries. However, facts tell us: this youth is so easy to pass away, this flame is so easy to extinguish.

Tianyi's new film "Flames of Youth" is premiering at Carlton. I don't need to advertise it here regarding how superb the director is and how realistic the expressions are, but at least it will give every pursuer of the flame of youth a little inspiration. Happy friends, please bring your loved ones here and put the flame of youth into your hearts, because there is poetry here, there are paintings here, it can intoxicate your soul, it can beautify your life!

Film Novel

Common Hatred (2) 272

— Hui Lan

Zhi Chao seemed to have something to say, but he stammered and hesitated. Finally, he said, "I owe you so much for saving me this time, and I don't have much to repay you. I'm graduating from military academy this year, and my family has a little property. May I ask you to betroth Xiaofen to me?"

Gui Sheng thought for a while and suddenly said, "Your injury has healed, and this place is very simple and slow. Please be on your way tomorrow!"

Zhi Chao was unexpectedly disappointed. Looking inside, Xiaofen walked step by step to Gui Sheng's side, looking at the expressions on their faces, then slowly lowered her head. From disappointment to pain, Xiaofen's tears were almost about to fall. Zhi Chao looked at this situation and helplessly lowered his head and walked out of the door. Gui Sheng saw Zhi Chao lingering outside the door, turned his head and said softly to Xiaofen, "Don't take it seriously. This is just a temporary whim of the rich. Forcing a marriage will definitely not end well in the future." The moonlight was so cold, Zhi Chao wandered back and forth, and Xiaofen slowly approached him, silently unable to speak. Zhi Chao stroked Xiaofen's shoulder and sat on the stone bench. Xiaofen looked at him with tears in her eyes, again and again. Zhi Chao seemed to have thought of something, leaned close to her ear, and whispered. Xiaofen shook her head firmly in surprise. Zhi Chao held her hand tightly and whispered again.

"Then what about Dad alone?" she asked. Zhi Chao knew she had been swayed, so he told her his remedy. Xiaofen finally nodded shyly in agreement. The two looked at each other affectionately.

The moonlight shone in from the window. Gui Sheng was already fast asleep. Zhi Chao and Xiaofen were packing their luggage, secretly pushing open the door and going out. The shadows of the two quickly disappeared on the ground. The alarm clock rang, and Gui Sheng woke up from his dream. Seeing the door wide open, he knew something was wrong. He quickly turned back inside, but Xiaofen was nowhere to be found. He ran out, but the train had already passed through the gate. Zhi Chao and Xiaofen in the second-class carriage made him angry, and two tears flowed from his old eyes.

The transformation started from the bottom. Xiaofen's feet had changed from cloth shoes to embroidered shoes, and then from embroidered shoes to high heels. Naturally, her clothes had changed from short jackets to cheongsams, and her hair had naturally been cut.

A orderly came in and handed over a calling card. Zhi Chao looked at the calling card and happily walked to Xiaofen. "This is my fellow villager Yue Xue, and also my current direct superior, Chief of Staff Wang Zhen'an. Come out and meet him in a while!"

At this time, Xiaofen's hometown was experiencing a flood in the late autumn season! Everything was flooded. Gui Sheng was mixed among the disaster victims, scrambling to climb onto the train to escape for his life.

At this time, Xiaofen was not the same as before. Slender eyebrows, curly hair, she could actually follow Wang Zhen'an and Li Zhi Chao into the bustling, intoxicating dance hall. Zhang Manlin, a social star, was a queen who dominated men. She stood up happily, ordered a group of boyfriends, everyone to have a drink, suddenly saw Zhen'an, left all her boyfriends, walked over, greeted Zhen'an very affectionately, unceremoniously pulled out a chair, sat next to Zhen'an, turned to look at Zhi Chao, and signaled Zhen'an to introduce him to her.
